<p><b>Aalen</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈʔaːlən]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen2.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/Aalen2.ogg" class="internal" title="Aalen2.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>) is a former <a href="/wiki/Free_Imperial_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Imperial City">Free Imperial City</a> located in the eastern part of the German state of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, about 70 kilometres (43&#160;mi) east of <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a> and 48 kilometres (30&#160;mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Ulm" title="Ulm">Ulm</a>. It is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Ostalbkreis" title="Ostalbkreis">Ostalbkreis</a> district and is its largest town. It is also the largest town in the <a href="/wiki/Ostw%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Ostwürttemberg">Ostwürttemberg</a> region. Since 1956, Aalen has had the status of <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fe_Kreisstadt" title="Große Kreisstadt">Große Kreisstadt</a> (major district town). It is noted for its many <a href="/wiki/Half-timbered" class="mw-redirect" title="Half-timbered">half-timbered</a> houses constructed from the 16th century through the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-munro_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-munro-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>With an area of 146.63&#160;km<sup>2</sup>, Aalen is ranked 7th in Baden-Württemberg and 2nd within the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_(region)" title="Stuttgart (region)">Government Region of Stuttgart</a>, after Stuttgart. With a population of about 66,000, Aalen is the 15th most-populated settlement in Baden-Württemberg.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Situation">Situation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Situation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_Luftbild.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Aalen_Luftbild.JPG/220px-Aalen_Luftbild.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Aalen_Luftbild.JPG/330px-Aalen_Luftbild.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Aalen_Luftbild.JPG/440px-Aalen_Luftbild.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_Luftbild.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of the district of Unterkochen (the town centre is partly covered and in the background), the Aalen lowlands well perceptible in the back</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aalen is situated on the upper reaches of the river <a href="/wiki/Kocher" title="Kocher">Kocher</a>, at the foot of the <a href="/wiki/Swabian_Jura" title="Swabian Jura">Swabian Jura</a> which lies to the south and south-east, and close to the hilly landscapes of the <a href="/wiki/Ellwangen_Hills" title="Ellwangen Hills">Ellwangen Hills</a> to the north and the <i>Welland</i> to the north-west.</p>
<p>The west of Aalen's territory is on the foreland of the eastern Swabian Jura, and the north and north-west is on the <a href="/wiki/Swabian-Franconian_Forest" title="Swabian-Franconian Forest">Swabian-Franconian Forest</a>, both being part of the <a href="/wiki/Swabian_Keuper-Lias_Plains" title="Swabian Keuper-Lias Plains">Swabian Keuper-Lias Plains</a>. The south-west is part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Albuch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Albuch (page does not exist)">Albuch</a>, the east is part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=H%C3%A4rtsfeld&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Härtsfeld (page does not exist)">Härtsfeld</a>, these two both being parts of the Swabian Jura.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Kocher enters the town's territory from <a href="/wiki/Oberkochen" title="Oberkochen">Oberkochen</a> to the south, crosses the district of Unterkochen, then enters the town centre, where the <i>Aal</i> flows into it. The <i>Aal</i> is a small river located only within the town's territory. Next, the Kocher crosses the district of Wasseralfingen, then leaves the town for <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCttlingen,_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Hüttlingen, Baden-Württemberg">Hüttlingen</a>. Rivers originating near Aalen are the <a href="/wiki/Rems" title="Rems">Rems</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Essingen" class="mw-redirect" title="Essingen">Essingen</a>, west of Aalen) and the <a href="/wiki/Jagst" title="Jagst">Jagst</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Unterschneidheim" title="Unterschneidheim">Unterschneidheim</a>, east of Aalen), both being tributaries of the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a>, just like the Kocher.</p>
<p>The elevation in the centre of the market square is 430 metres (1,410&#160;ft) relative to <a href="/wiki/Normalh%C3%B6hennull" title="Normalhöhennull">Normalhöhennull</a>. The territory's lowest point is at the <a href="/wiki/Lein_(Kocher)" title="Lein (Kocher)">Lein</a> river near Rodamsdörfle, the highest point is the Grünberg's peak near Unterkochen at 733 metres (2,405&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-bauer9_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer9-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aalen's territory ranges over all <a href="/wiki/Group_(stratigraphy)" title="Group (stratigraphy)">lithostratigraphic groups</a> of the <a href="/wiki/South_German_Jurassic" title="South German Jurassic">South German Jurassic</a>: Aalen's south and the <i>Flexner</i> massif are on top of the <a href="/wiki/White_Jurassic" title="White Jurassic">White Jurassic</a>, the town centre is on the <a href="/wiki/Brown_Jurassic" title="Brown Jurassic">Brown Jurassic</a>, and a part of Wasseralfingen is on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Jurassic" title="Black Jurassic">Black Jurassic</a>. As a result, the town advertises itself as a "Geologist's Mecca".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most parts of the territory are on the <i>Opalinuston-Formation</i> (Opalinum Clay <a href="/wiki/Formation_(stratigraphy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Formation (stratigraphy)">Formation</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/Aalenian" title="Aalenian">Aalenian</a> subdivision of the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> Period, which is named after Aalen.<sup id="cite_ref-munro_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-munro-2">[2]</a></sup> On the <i>Sandberg</i>, the <i>Schnaitberg</i> and the <i>Schradenberg</i> hills, all in the west of Aalen, the <i>Eisensandstein</i> (Iron Sandstone) formation emerges to the surface. On the other hills of the city, <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sands</a> <i>(Goldshöfer Sande)</i>, <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravel</a> and residual <a href="/wiki/Rubble" title="Rubble">rubble</a> prevail. The historic centre of Aalen and the other areas in the Kocher valley are founded completely on <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">holocenic</a> <a href="/wiki/Floodplain" title="Floodplain">floodplain</a> <a href="/wiki/Loam" title="Loam">loam</a> <i>(Auelehm)</i> and riverbed gravel that have filled in the valley.</p>
<p>Most parts of Dewangen and Fachsenfeld are founded on formations of <i>Jurensismergel</i> (Jurensis <a href="/wiki/Marl" title="Marl">Marl</a>), <i>Posidonienschiefer</i> (cf. <a href="/wiki/Posidonia_Shale" title="Posidonia Shale">Posidonia Shale</a>), <i>Amaltheenton</i> (Amalthean Clay), <i>Numismalismergel</i> (Numismalis Marl) and <i>Obtususton</i> (Obtusus Clay, named after <a href="/wiki/Asteroceras_obtusum" title="Asteroceras obtusum">Asteroceras obtusum</a> ammonites) moving from south to north, all belonging to the Jurassic and being rich in fossils. They are at last followed by the <i>Trossingen Formation</i> already belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Late_Triassic" title="Late Triassic">Late Triassic</a>.</p>
<p>Until 1939 iron ore was mined on the <i>Braunenberg</i> hill. (see <a href="#Tiefer_Stollen">Tiefer Stollen</a> section).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent_of_the_borough">Extent of the borough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Extent of the borough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The maximum extent of the town's territory amounts to 18 kilometres (11&#160;mi) in a north-south dimension and 25 kilometres (16&#160;mi) in an east-west dimension. The area is 14,662.8 hectares (36,233 acres), which includes 42.2% 6,186.2 hectares (15,286 acres) agriculturally used area and 37.7% 5,534.9 hectares (13,677 acres) of forest. 11.5% 1,692.3 hectares (4,182 acres) are built up or vacant, 6.4% 932.8 hectares (2,305 acres) is used by traffic infrastructure. Sporting and recreation grounds and parks comprise 1% 152.7 hectares (377 acres), other areas 1.1% 163.9 hectares (405 acres).<sup id="cite_ref-stat._Jahrbuch_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat._Jahrbuch-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_towns">Adjacent towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Adjacent towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following municipalities border on Aalen. They are listed clockwise, beginning south, with their respective linear distances to Aalen town centre given in brackets:</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oberkochen" title="Oberkochen">Oberkochen</a> (6&#160;km or 3.7&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Essingen_(W%C3%BCrttemberg)" title="Essingen (Württemberg)">Essingen</a> (6&#160;km or 3.7&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Heuchlingen" title="Heuchlingen">Heuchlingen</a> (11&#160;km or 6.8&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Abtsgm%C3%BCnd" title="Abtsgmünd">Abtsgmünd</a> (9&#160;km or 5.6&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Neuler" title="Neuler">Neuler</a> (10&#160;km or 6.2&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCttlingen_(W%C3%BCrttemberg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hüttlingen (Württemberg)">Hüttlingen</a> (6&#160;km or 3.7&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Rainau" title="Rainau">Rainau</a> (10&#160;km or 6.2&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Westhausen_(W%C3%BCrttemberg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westhausen (Württemberg)">Westhausen</a> (9&#160;km or 5.6&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Lauchheim" title="Lauchheim">Lauchheim</a> (12&#160;km or 7.5&#160;mi), <a href="/wiki/Bopfingen" title="Bopfingen">Bopfingen</a> (20&#160;km or 12&#160;mi) and <a href="/wiki/Neresheim" title="Neresheim">Neresheim</a> (20&#160;km or 12&#160;mi), all in the <a href="/wiki/Ostalbkreis" title="Ostalbkreis">Ostalbkreis</a> district, furthermore <a href="/wiki/Heidenheim_an_der_Brenz" title="Heidenheim an der Brenz">Heidenheim an der Brenz</a> (18&#160;km or 11&#160;mi) and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsbronn" title="Königsbronn">Königsbronn</a> (10&#160;km or 6.2&#160;mi), both in <a href="/wiki/Heidenheim_(district)" title="Heidenheim (district)">Heidenheim district</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughs">Boroughs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Boroughs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png/220px-Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png/330px-Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png/440px-Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png 2x" data-file-width="1111" data-file-height="842" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_Stadtbezirke.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Aalen's boroughs <i>(Stadtbezirke)</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aalen's territory consists of the town centre <i>(Kernstadt)</i> and the municipalities <a href="/wiki/Merger_(politics)" title="Merger (politics)">merged</a> from between 1938 (Unterrombach) and 1975 (Wasseralfingen, see <a href="#Mergings">mergings</a> section). The municipalities merged in the course of the latest municipal reform of the 1970s are also called <i><a href="/wiki/Stadtbezirk" title="Stadtbezirk">Stadtbezirke</a></i> (quarters or districts), and are <i>Ortschaften</i> ("settlements") in terms of Baden-Württemberg's <i><a href="/wiki/Gemeindeordnung" title="Gemeindeordnung">Gemeindeordnung</a></i> (municipal code), which means, each of them has its own council elected by its respective residents <i>(Ortschaftsrat)</i> and is presided by a spokesperson <i>(Ortsvorsteher)</i>.</p>
<p>The town centre itself and the merged former municipalities consist of numerous villages <i>(Teilorte)</i>, mostly separated by open ground from each other and having their own independent and long-standing history. Some however have been created as <a href="/wiki/Planned_community" title="Planned community">planned communities</a>, which were given proper names, but no well-defined borders.</p>
<p>List of villages:<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>

</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spatial_planning">Spatial planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Spatial planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aalen forms a <i>Mittelzentrum</i> ("medium-level centre") within the <a href="/wiki/Ostw%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Ostwürttemberg">Ostwürttemberg</a> region. Its designated <a href="/wiki/Catchment_area_(human_geography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catchment area (human geography)">catchment area</a> includes the following municipalities of the central and eastern Ostalbkreis district: <a href="/wiki/Abtsgm%C3%BCnd" title="Abtsgmünd">Abtsgmünd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bopfingen" title="Bopfingen">Bopfingen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essingen_(W%C3%BCrttemberg)" title="Essingen (Württemberg)">Essingen</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCttlingen_(W%C3%BCrttemberg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hüttlingen (Württemberg)">Hüttlingen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirchheim_am_Ries" title="Kirchheim am Ries">Kirchheim am Ries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauchheim" title="Lauchheim">Lauchheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neresheim" title="Neresheim">Neresheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oberkochen" title="Oberkochen">Oberkochen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riesb%C3%BCrg" title="Riesbürg">Riesbürg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westhausen_(W%C3%BCrttemberg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westhausen (Württemberg)">Westhausen</a>, and is interwoven with the catchment area of <a href="/wiki/N%C3%B6rdlingen" title="Nördlingen">Nördlingen</a>, situated in <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, 30 kilometres (19&#160;mi) east of Aalen.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As Aalen's territory sprawls on escarpments of the Swabian Jura, on the Albuch and the Härtsfeld landscapes, and its elevation has a range of 355 metres (1,165&#160;ft), the climate varies from district to district.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Weather_station" title="Weather station">weather station</a> the following data originate from is located between the town centre and Wasseralfingen at about <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Aalen&amp;params=48_51_02_N_10_05_44_E_&amp;title=weather+station"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">48°51′02″N</span> <span class="longitude">10°05′44″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">48.85056°N 10.09556°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">48.85056; 10.09556</span></span><span style="display:none">﻿ (<span class="fn org">weather station</span>)</span></span></span></a></span> and has been in operation since 1991.</p>
<p>The sunshine duration is about 1800 hours per year, which averages 4.93 hours per day. So Aalen is above the German average of 1550 hours per year. However, with 167 days of <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a>, Aalen's region also ranks above the German average of 138. The annual rainfall is 807 millimetres (31.8&#160;in), which places Aalen in the middle within Baden-Württemberg.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The annual mean temperature is 9.9&#160;°C (49.8&#160;°F). Here Aalen ranks above the German average of 8.2&#160;°C (46.8&#160;°F) and the Baden-Württemberg average of 8.1&#160;°C (46.6&#160;°F).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civic_history">Civic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Civic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_settlements">First settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: First settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Numerous remains of early civilization have been found in the area. Tools made of <a href="/wiki/Flint" title="Flint">flint</a> and traces of <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> human settlement dated between the 8th and 5th millennium BC were found on several sites on the margins of the Kocher and Jagst valleys. On the <i>Schloßbaufeld</i> plateau (appr. 650 by 350 metres (2,130 by 1,150&#160;ft)), situated behind <i>Kocherburg</i> castle near Unterkochen, a hill-top settlement was found, with the core being dated to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. In the <i>Appenwang</i> forest near Wasseralfingen, in Goldshöfe, and in Ebnat, <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">tumuli</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Hallstatt_culture" title="Hallstatt culture">Hallstatt culture</a> were found. In Aalen and Wasseralfingen, gold and silver coins left by the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> were found. The Celts were responsible for the fortifications in the Schloßbaufeld settlement consisting of sectional embankments and a stone wall. Also, Near Heisenberg (Wasseralfingen), a Celtic <a href="/wiki/Nemeton" title="Nemeton">nemeton</a> has been identified; however it is no longer readily apparent.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer25_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer25-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_era">Roman era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Roman era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg/220px-Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg/330px-Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg/440px-Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Limesmuseum_Aalen_principia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Roman fort's excavated foundation walls</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After abandoning the <a href="/wiki/Alb_Limes" title="Alb Limes">Alb Limes</a> (a <i><a href="/wiki/Limes" title="Limes">limes</a></i> generally following the ridgeline of the Swabian Jura) around 150 <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>, Aalen's territory became part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, in direct vicinity of the then newly erected <a href="/wiki/Rhaetian_Limes" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhaetian Limes">Rhaetian Limes</a>. The Romans erected a <a href="/wiki/Castrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Castrum">castrum</a> to house the <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> unit <i><a href="/wiki/Ala_(Roman_military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ala (Roman military)">Ala</a> II Flavia milliaria</i>; its remains are known today as <i>Kastell Aalen</i> ("Aalen Roman fort"). The site is west of today's town centre at the bottom of the <i>Schillerhöhe</i> hill. With about 1,000 horsemen and nearly as many <a href="/wiki/Groom_(horse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Groom (horse)">grooms</a>, it was the greatest fort of <a href="/wiki/Auxiliaries_(Roman_military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Auxiliaries (Roman military)">auxiliaries</a> along the Rhaetian Limes. There were Civilian settlements adjacent along the south and the east. Around 260 AD, the Romans gave up the fort as they withdrew their presence in unoccupied <a href="/wiki/Germania" title="Germania">Germania</a> back to the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> rivers, and the <a href="/wiki/Alamanni" class="mw-redirect" title="Alamanni">Alamanni</a> took over the region.<sup id="cite_ref-ostalbkreis_315_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ostalbkreis_315-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aalen-antike_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aalen-antike-22">[22]</a></sup> Based on 3rd- and 4th-century coins found, the civilian settlement continued to exist for the time being. However, there is no evidence of continued civilization between the Roman era and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer25_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer25-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Based on discovery of alamannic graves, archaeologists have established the 7th century as the origination of Aalen. In the northern and western walls of St. John's church, which is located directly adjacent to the eastern gate of the Roman fort, Roman stones were incorporated. The building that exists today probably dates to the 9th century.</p>
<p>The first mention of Aalen was in 839, when emperor <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a> reportedly permitted the <a href="/wiki/Fulda_monastery" title="Fulda monastery">Fulda monastery</a> to exchange land with the Hammerstadt village, then known as <i>Hamarstat</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ostalbkreis_123_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ostalbkreis_123-23">[23]</a></sup> Aalen itself was first mentioned in an inventory list of <a href="/wiki/Ellwangen_Abbey" title="Ellwangen Abbey">Ellwangen Abbey</a>, dated ca. 1136, as the village <i>Alon</i>, along with a lower nobleman named Conrad of Aalen. This nobleman probably had his ancestral castle at a site south of today's town centre and was subject first to Ellwangen abbey, later to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenstaufen" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Hohenstaufen">House of Hohenstaufen</a>, and eventually to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Oettingen" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Oettingen">House of Oettingen</a>. 1426 was the last time a member of that house was mentioned in connection with Aalen. Documents, from the Middle Ages, indicate that the town of Aalen was founded by the Hohenstaufen some time between 1241 and 1246, but at a different location than the earlier village, which was supposedly destroyed in 1388 during the war between the Alliance of Swabian Cities and the Dukes of Bavaria. Later, it is documented that the counts of Oettingen ruled the town in 1340. They are reported to have pawned the town to Count <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_II,_Count_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Eberhard II, Count of Württemberg">Eberhard II</a> and subsequently to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="House of Württemberg">House of Württemberg</a> in 1358 or 1359 in exchange for an amount of money.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_City">Imperial City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Imperial City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Designation_as_Imperial_City">Designation as Imperial City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Designation as Imperial City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>During the war against Württemberg, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles IV</a> took the town without a fight after a siege. On 3 December 1360, he declared Aalen an <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">Imperial City</a>, that is, a city or town responsible only to the emperor, a status that made it a quasi-sovereign city-state and that it kept until 1803.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1377, Aalen joined the Alliance of Swabian Cities, and in 1385, the term <i>civitas</i> appears in the town's seal for the first time. In 1398, Aalen was granted the right to hold markets, and in 1401 Aalen obtained proper jurisdiction.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_1528.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Aalen_1528.jpg/220px-Aalen_1528.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Aalen_1528.jpg/330px-Aalen_1528.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Aalen_1528.jpg/440px-Aalen_1528.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1681" data-file-height="1209" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_1528.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Town view of 1528</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The oldest artistic representation of Aalen was made in 1528. It was made as the basis of a lawsuit between the town and the Counts of Oettingen at the <a href="/wiki/Reichskammergericht" title="Reichskammergericht">Reichskammergericht</a> in Speyer. It shows Aalen surrounded by walls, towers, and double moats. The layout of the moats, which had an embankment built between them, is recognizable by the present streets named <i>Nördlicher, Östlicher, Südlicher</i> and <i>Westlicher Stadtgraben</i> (Northern, Eastern, Southern and Western Moat respectively). The wall was about 6 metres (20&#160;ft) tall, 1518 <a href="/wiki/Pace_(unit)" title="Pace (unit)">single paces</a> (990 metres (3,250&#160;ft)) long and enclosed an area of 5.3 hectares (13 acres). During its early years, the town had two <a href="/wiki/Town_gate" class="mw-redirect" title="Town gate">town gates</a>: The <i>Upper</i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Ellwangen" title="Ellwangen">Ellwangen</a> Gate</i> in the east, and St. Martin's gate in the south; however due to frequent floods, St. Martin's gate was bricked up in the 14th century and replaced by the <i>Lower</i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Schw%C3%A4bisch_Gm%C3%BCnd" title="Schwäbisch Gmünd">Gmünd</a> Gate</i> built in the west before 1400. Later, several minor side gates were added. The central street market took place on the <i>Wettegasse</i> (today called <i>Marktplatz</i>, "market square") and the <i>Reichsstädter Straße</i>. So the market district stretched from one gate to the other, however in Aalen it was not straight, but with a 90-degree curve between southern (St. Martin's) gate and eastern (Ellwangen) gate.</p>
<p>Around 1500, the civic graveyard was relocated from the town church to St. John's Church,<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> and in 1514, the <i>Vierundzwanziger</i> ("Group of 24") was the first assembly constituted by the citizens.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Reformation">Reformation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Reformation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Delegated by Württemberg's Duke <a href="/wiki/Louis_III,_Duke_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Louis III, Duke of Württemberg">Louis III</a>, on 28 June 1575, nearly 30 years after <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>'s death, <a href="/wiki/Jakob_Andreae" title="Jakob Andreae">Jakob Andreae</a>, professor and chancellor of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_T%C3%BCbingen" title="University of Tübingen">University of Tübingen</a>, arrived in Aalen. The sermon he gave the following day convinced the mayor, the council, and the citizens to adopt the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> in the town. Andreae stayed in Aalen for four weeks to help with the change.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> This brought along enormous changes, as the council forbade the Roman Catholic priests to celebrate masses and give sermons. However, after victories of the imperial armies at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prince-Provost" title="Prince-Provost">Prince-Provostry</a> of Ellwangen, which still held the <a href="/wiki/Jus_patronatus" title="Jus patronatus">right of patronage</a> in Aalen, were able to temporarily bring Catholicism back to Aalen; however after the military successes of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Union" title="Protestant Union">Protestant Union</a>, Protestant church practices were instituted again.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_of_1634">Fire of 1634</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fire of 1634">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>On the night of 5 September 1634,<sup id="cite_ref-GA_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA-26">[26]</a></sup> two ensigns of the army of <a href="/wiki/Bernard_of_Saxe-Weimar" title="Bernard of Saxe-Weimar">Bernard of Saxe-Weimar</a> who were fighting with the Swedes and retreating after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_N%C3%B6rdlingen_(1634)" title="Battle of Nördlingen (1634)">Battle of Nördlingen</a> set fire to two powder carriages, to prevent the war material to fall into Croatian hands and to prevent their advance. The result was a conflagration, that some say destroyed portions of the town. There are differing stories regarding this fire. According to 17th-century accounts, the church and all the buildings, except of the <i>Schwörturm</i> tower, were casualties of the fire, and only nine families survived. 19th century research by Hermann Bauer, Lutheran pastor and local historian, discovered that the 17th-century account is exaggerated, but he does agree that the town church and buildings in a "rather large" semicircle around it were destroyed. The fire also destroyed the town archive housed in an addition to the church, with all of its documents.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> After the fire, soldiers of both armies went through the town looting.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> It took nearly 100 years for the town to reach its population of 2,000.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG/220px-Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG/330px-Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG/440px-Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Free_Imperial_City_of_Aalen.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Territory of the Imperial City of Aalen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>French troops marched through Aalen in 1688 during the <a href="/wiki/Nine_Years%27_War" title="Nine Years' War">Nine Years' War</a>; however, unlike other places, they left without leaving severe damages. The French came through again in 1702 during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> and in 1741 during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> the latter also caused imperial troops to move through in 1743.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The town church's tower collapsed in 1765, presumably because proper building techniques were not utilized during the reconstruction after the fire of 1634. The collapsing tower struck two children of the tower watchman who died of their injuries, and destroyed the nave, leaving only the altar cross intact. The remaining walls had to be knocked down due to the damage. Reconstruction began the same year, creating the building that exists today.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 November 1749, the so-called <i>Aalen protocol</i> regulating the cohabitation of Lutherans and Roman Catholics in the jointly ruled territory of Oberkochen was signed in Aalen by the Duchy of Württemberg and the Prince-Provostry of Ellwangen. Aalen had been chosen because of its neutral status as a Free Imperial City.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Napoleonic_era_and_end_of_the_Imperial_City_of_Aalen">Napoleonic era and end of the Imperial City of Aalen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Napoleonic era and end of the Imperial City of Aalen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg/220px-Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg/330px-Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg/440px-Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="1234" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Angriff_auf_Aalen_1796.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
French attack on Aalen of 1796</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_First_Coalition" title="War of the First Coalition">War of the First Coalition</a> (1796), Aalen was looted.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> The War of the Second Coalition concluded in 1801 with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lun%C3%A9ville" title="Treaty of Lunéville">Treaty of Lunéville</a>, which led to the <a href="/wiki/German_Mediatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="German Mediatisation">German Mediatisation</a> of 1803 that assigned most Imperial Cities to the neighbouring principalities. Aalen was assigned to the <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">electorate</a> of Württemberg, which later became the Kingdom of Württemberg, and became seat of the District ("Oberamt") of Aalen. During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Third_Coalition" title="War of the Third Coalition">War of the Third Coalition</a>, on 6 October 1805, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> arrived in Aalen, with an army of 40,000. This event, along with Bavarian and Austrian troops moving in some days later, caused miseries that according to the town clerk "no feather could describe".<sup id="cite_ref-bauer145_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer145-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1811, the municipality of Unterrombach was formed out of some villages previously belonging to Aalen, some to the Barons of Wöllwarth, and the eastern villages were assigned to the municipality of Unterkochen.</p>
<p>In the age of the Napoleonic wars, the <a href="/wiki/Town_wall" class="mw-redirect" title="Town wall">town walls</a> were no longer of use, and in the 18th century, with the maintenance of walls, gates and towers becoming more neglected Finally, due to the fact that the funds were lacking, starting in 1800, most towers were demolished, the other buildings followed soon.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer145_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer145-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_revolution">Industrial revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Industrial revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_nach_1861.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Aalen_nach_1861.jpg/220px-Aalen_nach_1861.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Aalen_nach_1861.jpg/330px-Aalen_nach_1861.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Aalen_nach_1861.jpg/440px-Aalen_nach_1861.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1252" data-file-height="1097" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_nach_1861.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Railway station and town after 1861</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a>, Aalen's economy was shaped by its rural setting. Many citizens were pursuing farming besides their craft, such as <a href="/wiki/Tanning_(leather)" title="Tanning (leather)">tanning</a>. In the mid 19th century, there were twelve tanneries in Aalen, due to the proximity of <a href="/wiki/Ulm" title="Ulm">Ulm</a>, an important sales market. Other crafts that added to the economy were <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving mills</a>, which produced linen and woolen goods, and baking of sweet pastry and gingerbread.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer122_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer122-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eb1911_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eb1911-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Aalen, industrialisation was a slow process. The first major increase was in the 1840s, when three factories for <a href="/wiki/Nail_(fastener)" title="Nail (fastener)">nails</a> and some other factories emerged.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer122_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer122-30">[30]</a></sup> It was the link with the railway network, by the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Rems_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Rems Railway">Rems Railway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cannstatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannstatt">Cannstatt</a> to Wasseralfingen in 1861, that brought more industry to Aalen, along with the royal <a href="/wiki/Steel_mill" title="Steel mill">steel mill</a> (later <i>Schwäbische Hüttenwerke</i>) in Wasseralfingen. The Rems Railway's extension to Nördlingen in 1863, the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Brenz_Railway" title="Brenz Railway">Brenz Railway</a> in 1864 and of the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Jagst_Railway" title="Upper Jagst Railway">Upper Jagst Railway</a> in 1866 turned Aalen into a <a href="/wiki/Railway_hub" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway hub">railway hub</a>. Furthermore, between 1901 and its shutdown in 1972, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=H%C3%A4rtsfeld_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Härtsfeld Railway (page does not exist)">Härtsfeld Railway</a> connected Aalen with <a href="/wiki/Dillingen_an_der_Donau" title="Dillingen an der Donau">Dillingen an der Donau</a> via <a href="/wiki/Neresheim" title="Neresheim">Neresheim</a>. Part of becoming a rail hub entailed more jobs based on the rail industry. These included, a maintenance facility, a <a href="/wiki/Roundhouse" title="Roundhouse">roundhouse</a>, an administrative office, two track maintenance shops, and a freight station with an industrial <a href="/wiki/Branch_line" title="Branch line">branch line</a>. This helped shape Aalen into what today's historians call a "railwayman's town".<sup id="cite_ref-Hafner_Stadtf.C3.BChrer_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hafner_Stadtf.C3.BChrer-32">[32]</a></sup> Starting in 1866, the utilities in town all began to be upgraded. Starting with the Aalen <a href="/wiki/Gasworks" title="Gasworks">gasworks</a> which were opened and <a href="/wiki/Gas_lighting" title="Gas lighting">gas lighting</a> was introduced. Then in 1870, a modern <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a> system was started and in 1912 the <a href="/wiki/Mains_electricity" title="Mains electricity">mains electricity</a>. Finally, in 1935, the first electrically powered <a href="/wiki/Street_light" title="Street light">street lights</a> were installed.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer122_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer122-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen-um-1900.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aalen-um-1900.jpg/220px-Aalen-um-1900.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aalen-um-1900.jpg/330px-Aalen-um-1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Aalen-um-1900.jpg/440px-Aalen-um-1900.jpg 2x" data-file-width="649" data-file-height="427" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen-um-1900.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aalen by 1900</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To fight housing shortage during and immediately after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the town set up barracks settlement areas at the <i>Schlauch</i> and <i>Alter Turnplatz</i> grounds. In spite of the industry being crippled by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> of 1929, the public baths at the Hirschbach creek where modernized, extended and re-opened in 1931.<sup id="cite_ref-Hafner_Stadtf.C3.BChrer_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hafner_Stadtf.C3.BChrer-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nazi_era">Nazi era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Nazi era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_November_1932" title="German federal election, November 1932">federal election of 1932</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> performed below average in Aalen with 25.8% of votes compared to 33.1% on the national level, thus finishing second to the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Germany)" title="Centre Party (Germany)">Centre Party</a> which had 26.6% (11.9% nationwide) of the votes, and ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> with 19.8% (20.4%). However, the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_March_1933" title="German federal election, March 1933">March 1933 federal elections</a> showed that the sentiment had changed as the Nazi Party received 34.1% (still below German average 43.9% nationwide), but by far the leading vote-getter in Aalen, followed by the Centre party at 26.6% (11.3% nationwide) and the Social Democrats 18.6% (18.3% nationwide).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The democratically elected mayor Friedrich Schwarz remained in office until the Nazis removed him from office, in 1934, and replaced him by chairman of the Nazi Party town council head and brewery owner Karl Barth. Karl Barth was a provisional mayor until the more permanent solution of Karl Schübel. In August 1934, the Nazi consumer fair <a href="/w/index.php?title=Braune_Messe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Braune Messe (page does not exist)">Braune Messe</a> ("brown fair") was held in Aalen.<sup id="cite_ref-Braune_Messe_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braune_Messe-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi rule in Germany</a>, there were many military offices constructed in Aalen, starting with, in 1936, a <a href="/wiki/Military_district_(Germany)" title="Military district (Germany)">military district</a> riding and driving school. The Nazis also built an army replenishment office <i>(Heeresverpflegungsamt)</i>, a branch arsenal office <i>(Heeresnebenzeugamt)</i> and a branch army ammunitions institute <i>(Heeresnebenmunitionsanstalt)</i>.</p>
<p>Starting in 1935, <a href="/wiki/Merger_(politics)" title="Merger (politics)">mergers</a> of neighbouring towns began. In 1938, the Oberamt was transformed into the <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Germany" title="Districts of Germany">Landkreis</a> of Aalen and the municipality of Unterrombach was disbanded. Its territory was mostly added to Aalen, with the exception of Hammerstadt, which was added to the municipality of Dewangen. Forst, Rauental and Vogelsang were added to Essingen (in 1952 the entire former municipality of Unterrombach was merged into Aalen, with the exception of Forst, which is part of Essingen until present).</p>
<p>In September 1944, the <i>Wiesendorf</i> <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">concentration camp</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_subcamps_of_Natzweiler-Struthof" title="List of subcamps of Natzweiler-Struthof">subcamp</a> of <a href="/wiki/Natzweiler-Struthof" title="Natzweiler-Struthof">Natzweiler-Struthof</a>, was constructed nearby. It was designated for between 200 and 300 prisoners who were utilized for <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">forced labor in industrial businesses</a> nearby. Until the camp's dissolution in February 1945, 60 prisoners died.<sup id="cite_ref-Sch.C3.A4tzle_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sch.C3.A4tzle-35">[35]</a></sup> Between 1946 and 1957, the camp buildings were torn down; however, its foundations are still in place in house <i>Moltkestraße 44/46</i>. Also, there were several other labour camps which existed where prisoners of war along with women and men from occupied countries occupied by Germany were pooled. The prisoners at these other camps had to work for the arms industry in major businesses like <i>Schwäbische Hüttenwerke</i> and the <i>Alfing Keßler</i> machine factory.<sup id="cite_ref-gedenkstaetten_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gedenkstaetten-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the civic hospital, the <a href="/wiki/Deaconess" title="Deaconess">deaconesses</a> on duty were gradually replaced by <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_People%27s_Welfare" title="National Socialist People's Welfare">National Socialist People's Welfare</a> nurses. <a href="/wiki/Nazi_eugenics" title="Nazi eugenics">Nazi eugenics</a> led to <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">compulsory sterilization</a> of some 200 persons there.<sup id="cite_ref-Einhorn_140_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Einhorn_140-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fortunately, Aalen avoided most of the combat activity during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. It was only during the last weeks of the war that Aalen became a target of <a href="/wiki/Air_warfare_of_World_War_II" title="Air warfare of World War II">air warfare</a>, which led to the destruction and severe damage of parts of the town, the train station, and other railway installations. A series of air attacks lasting for more than three weeks reached its peak on 17 April 1945, when <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">United States Army Air Forces</a> planes bombed the branch arsenal office and the train station. During this raid, 59 people were killed, more than half of them buried by debris, and more than 500 lost their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-Aalen_Luftangriffe_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aalen_Luftangriffe-38">[38]</a></sup> Also, 33&#160;residential buildings, 12&#160;other buildings and 2&#160;bridges were destroyed, and 163&#160;buildings, including 2&#160;churches, were damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer145_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer145-29">[29]</a></sup> Five days later, the Nazi rulers of Aalen were unseated by the US forces.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_era">Post-war era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Post-war era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Aalen became part of the State of <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, upon its creation in 1952. Then, with the Baden-Württemberg territorial reform of 1973, the District of Aalen was merged into the <a href="/wiki/Ostalbkreis" title="Ostalbkreis">Ostalbkreis</a> district. Subsequently, Aalen became seat of that district, and in 1975, the town's borough attained its present size (<a href="#Mergings">see below</a>).</p>
<p>The population of Aalen exceeded the limit of 20,000, which was the requirement for to gain the status of <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fe_Kreisstadt" title="Große Kreisstadt">Große Kreisstadt</a> ("major district town") in 1946. On 1 August 1947, Aalen was declared <i>Unmittelbare Kreisstadt</i> ("immediate district town"), and with the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Gemeindeordnung" title="Gemeindeordnung">Gemeindeordnung</a> (municipal code) of Baden-Württemberg on 1 April 1956, it was declared <i>Große Kreisstadt</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 31 December 2008, 51.1&#160;percent of Aalen were members of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, 23.9&#160;percent were members of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical-Lutheran_Church_in_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Evangelical-Lutheran Church in Württemberg">Evangelical-Lutheran Church</a>. About 25&#160;percent belong to other or no religious community or gave no information.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The district of Waldhausen was the district with the highest percentage of Roman Catholic inhabitants at 75.6&#160;percent, and the central district was the one with the highest percentage of Evangelical-Lutheran inhabitants at 25.6&#160;percent, as well as those claiming no religious preference at 32.5&#160;percent.<sup id="cite_ref-stat._Jahrbuch_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat._Jahrbuch-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestantism">Protestantism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Protestantism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Aalen's population originally was subject to the <a href="/wiki/Jus_patronatus" title="Jus patronatus">jus patronatus</a> of Ellwangen Abbey, and thus subject to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Augsburg" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Augsburg">Roman Catholic Diocese of Augsburg</a>.</p>
<p>With the assistance of the Duke of Württemberg, in 1575, the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">reformation</a> was implemented in Aalen. Subsequently, Aalen has been a predominantly Protestant town for centuries, with the exception of the years from 1628 until 1632 (see <a href="#Reformation">reformation</a> section). Being an Imperial City, Aalen could govern its clerical matters on its own, so Clerics, organists and choir masters were direct subjects to the council, which thus exerted bishop-like power. There was even a proper hymn book for Aalen.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> After the transition to Württemberg, in 1803, Aalen became seat of a <a href="/wiki/Deanery" title="Deanery">deanery</a>, with the dean church being the Town Church (with the building constructed from 1765 to 1767 and existing until present). Another popular church is <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">St. John's</a> Church, located on the cemetery and refurbished in 1561.</p>
<p>As Aalen's population grew in the 20th century, more parishes were founded: <a href="/wiki/Mark_the_Evangelist" title="Mark the Evangelist">St. Mark's</a> parish with its church building of 1967 and <a href="/wiki/Martin_of_Tours" title="Martin of Tours">St. Martin's</a> parish with its church of 1974. In the borough of Unterrombach, Aalen had implemented the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">reformation</a> as well, but the community remained a <a href="/wiki/Chapel_of_ease" title="Chapel of ease">chapel-of-ease</a> of Aalen. A proper church, the Christ Church, was erected in 1912 and a proper parish was established in 1947. In Fachsenfeld, the ruling family of Woellwarth resp. of Leinroden implemented the reformation. A parish church was built in 1591, however with an influx of Catholics in the 18th century, a Catholic majority was established. The other districts of present-day Aalen remained mostly catholic after the reformation, however Wasseralfingen established a Lutheran parish in 1891 and a church, St. Magdalene's Church, in 1893. In Unterkochen, after World War II, a parish was established and a church was built in 1960. All four parishes belong to the deanery of Aalen within the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical-Lutheran_Church_in_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Evangelical-Lutheran Church in Württemberg">Evangelical-Lutheran Church in Württemberg</a>. Furthermore, in Aalen there are <a href="/wiki/Pietism" title="Pietism">Old Pietistic</a> communities.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Catholicism">Catholicism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Catholicism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg/170px-Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg/255px-Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg/340px-Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="467" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salvatorkirche_aalen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Salvator's Church</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The few Catholics of today's central district were covered by the parish of Unterkochen until the 19th century, a situation which continued for some years even after completion of <a href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">St. Mary's</a> Church in 1868, which was constructed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Georg_Morlok&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Georg Morlok (page does not exist)">Georg Morlok</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer145_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer145-29">[29]</a></sup> However, in 1872 Aalen got its proper parish again, and in 1913, a second Catholic church, Salvator's Church, was completed, and in 1969 the Holy Cross Church was also finished. In 1963, a second parish was set up, and in 1972 it got a new Church, the new St. Mary's Church, which has been erected in place of the old St. Mary's church, which had been torn down in 1968. Another church of the second parish was St. Augustine's Church, which was completed in 1970. Finally, in 1976 and 1988, St. Elizabeth's Church and St. Thomas' Church were completed. Furthermore, in 1963, the St. Michael pastoral care office was built.</p>
<p>Hofherrnweiler has its own Catholic church, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">St. Boniface's</a>, since 1904. The villages of Dewangen, Ebnat, Hofen, Waldhausen and Wasseralfingen had remained Catholic after reformation, so old parishes and churches persist there. The <i>Assumption of Mary</i> Church in Dewangen has an <a href="/wiki/Gothic_art" title="Gothic art">early Gothic</a> tower and a newly built nave (1875). <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Mary's Immaculate Conception</a> Church in Ebnat was constructed in 1723; however the church was first mentioned in 1298.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marienwallfahrtskirche_Unterkochen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marienwallfahrtskirche_Unterkochen.jpg/170px-Marienwallfahrtskirche_Unterkochen.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Marienwallfahrtskirche_Unterkochen.jpg/255px-Marienwallfahrtskirche_Unterkochen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a8/Marienwallfahrtskirche_Unterkochen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="264" data-file-height="397" /></a>

St. Mary, Unterkochen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hofen's <a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a>'s Church is a <a href="/wiki/Fortified_church" title="Fortified church">fortified church</a>, whose current nave was built between 1762 and 1775.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Alongside the church, the Late Gothic <a href="/wiki/Odile_of_Alsace" title="Odile of Alsace">St. Odile's</a> Chapel is standing, whose entrance has the year 1462 engraved upon it. Foundations of prior buildings have been dated to the 11th and 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>St. Mary's Church of Unterkochen was first mentioned in 1248, and has served the Catholics of Aalen for a long time. Waldhausen's parish church of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">St. Nicholas</a> was built between 1699 and 1716. Wasseralfingen at first was a <a href="/wiki/Chapel_of_ease" title="Chapel of ease">chapel of ease</a> for Hofen, but has since had its own chapel, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Stephen" title="Saint Stephen">St. Stephen</a>, built. It was presumably built in 1353 and remodeled in 1832. In 1834, a proper parish was established, which built a new St. Stephen's Church. This new building utilized the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_Revival_architecture" title="Romanesque Revival architecture">Romanesque Revival architecture</a> style and was built between 1881 and 1883, and has since remained the parish's landmark. Also, Fachsenfeld received its own church, named <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart" title="Sacred Heart">Sacred Heart</a> in 1895. All Catholic parishes within Aalen are today incorporated into four pastoral care units within the <i>Ostalb</i> Deanery of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Rottenburg-Stuttgart" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Rottenburg-Stuttgart">Diocese of Rottenburg-Stuttgart</a>; however these units also comprise some parishes outside of Aalen. Pastoral Care Unit two comprises the parishes of Essingen, Dewangen and Fachsenfeld, unit four comprises Hofen and Wasseralfingen, unit five comprises both parishes of Aalen's centre and Hofherrnweiler, unit five comprises Waldhausen, Ebnat, Oberkochen and Unterkochen.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_christian_communities">Other christian communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other christian communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In addition to the two major religions within Aalen, there are also <a href="/wiki/Free_church" title="Free church">free churches</a> and other communities, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_religions">Other religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Until the late 19th century, no <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a> were documented within Aalen. In 1886 there were four Jews were living in Aalen, a number that rose to ten in 1900, fell to seven in 1905, and remained so until 1925. Upon the Nazis' rise to power in 1933, seven Jews, including two children, lived in Aalen.<sup id="cite_ref-Juden_1984_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juden_1984-42">[42]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a> in 1938, the vitrines of the three Jewish shops in the town were smashed and their proprietors imprisoned for several weeks. After their release, most Aalen Jews emigrated. The last Jews of Aalen, Fanny Kahn, was forcibly resettled to <a href="/wiki/Oberdorf_am_Ipf" class="mw-redirect" title="Oberdorf am Ipf">Oberdorf am Ipf</a>, which had a large Jewish community. Today, a street of Aalen is named after her. The Jew Max Pfeffer returned from Brussels to Aalen in 1948 to continue his shop, but emigrated to Italy in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-Juden_1984_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juden_1984-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Aalen, there is an Islamic <a href="/wiki/Turkish-Islamic_Union_for_Religious_Affairs" title="Turkish-Islamic Union for Religious Affairs">Ditib</a> community, which maintains the <i>D.I.T.I.B. Mosque of Aalen (Central Mosque)</i> located at Ulmer Straße.<sup id="cite_ref-Moscheesuche_Ditib_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moscheesuche_Ditib-43">[43]</a></sup> The mosque's construction started on 30 August 2008. The <a href="/wiki/Mill%C3%AE_G%C3%B6r%C3%BC%C5%9F" title="Millî Görüş">Millî Görüş</a> organisation maintains the <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehmed II">Fatih</a> Mosque, as well at Ulmer Straße.<sup id="cite_ref-Moscheesuche_IGMG_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moscheesuche_IGMG-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mergings">Mergings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mergings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The present-day make up of Aalen was created on 21 June 1975 by the unification of the cities of Aalen and Wasseralfingen,<sup id="cite_ref-munro_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-munro-2">[2]</a></sup> with the initial name of <i>Aalen-Wasseralfingen</i>. This annexation made Aalen's territory one third larger than its prior size. On 1 July 1975, the name <i>Aalen</i> was revived. Prior to this merger, the town of Aalen had already annexed the following municipalities:</p>
<ul>
<li>1938: Unterrombach</li>
<li>1 January 1970: Waldhausen</li>
<li>1 July 1972: Ebnat</li>
<li>1 January 1973: Dewangen, Fachsenfeld (including the village of Hangendenbach, which was transferred from Abtsgmünd in 1954) and Unterkochen. The merging of Dewangen nearly doubled the territory of Aalen.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Population’s_progression_and_structure"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Population.E2.80.99s_progression_and_structure">Population’s progression and structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Population’s progression and structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_development_Aalen.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Population_development_Aalen.png/440px-Population_development_Aalen.png" width="440" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Population_development_Aalen.png/660px-Population_development_Aalen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Population_development_Aalen.png/880px-Population_development_Aalen.png 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="595" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_development_Aalen.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Progression of Aalen's population</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>, Aalen was just a small town with a few hundred inhabitants. The population grew slowly due to numerous wars, famines and epidemics. It was the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> in the 19th century where Aalen's growth accelerated. Whereas in 1803, only 1,932 people inhabited the town, in 1905 it had already increased to 10,442. The number continued to rise and reached 15,890 in 1939.</p>
<p>The influx of refugees and <a href="/wiki/Heimatvertriebene" title="Heimatvertriebene">ethnic Germans</a> from Germany's former eastern territories after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> pushed the population to 31,814 in 1961. The merger with Wasseralfingen on 21 June 1975 added 14,597 persons and resulted in a total population of 65,165 people. On 30 June 2005, the population, which was officially determined by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_statistical_offices_in_Germany" title="List of statistical offices in Germany">Statistical Office of Baden-Württemberg</a>, was 67,125.</p>
<p>The following overview shows how the population figures of the borough were ascertained. Until 1823, the figures are mostly estimates, thereafter census results or official updates by the state statistical office. Starting in 1871, the figures were determined by non-uniform method of tabulation using extrapolation.</p>

<p><small>¹ Census result</small></p>
<p>On 31 December 2008, Aalen had precisely 66,058 inhabitants, of which 33,579 were female and 32,479 were male. The average age of Aalen's inhabitants rose from 40.5 years in 2000 to 42.4 in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-stat._Jahrbuch_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat._Jahrbuch-6">[6]</a></sup> Within the borough, 6,312 foreigners resided, which is 9.56&#160;percent. Of them, the largest percentage are from <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (38&#160;percent of all foreigners), the second largest group are from Italy (13&#160;percent), followed by <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croatians</a> (6&#160;percent) and <a href="/wiki/Serb" class="mw-redirect" title="Serb">Serbs</a> (5&#160;percent).<sup id="cite_ref-stat._Jahrbuch_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat._Jahrbuch-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The number of married residents fell from 32,948 in 1996 to 31,357 in 2007, while the number of divorced residents rose in the same period from 2,625 to 3,859. The number of single residents slightly increased between 1996 and 2004 from 25,902 to 26,268 and fell slightly until 2007 to 26,147. The number of widowed residents fell from 5,036 in 1996 to 4,783 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-stat._Jahrbuch_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat._Jahrbuch-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Aalen has arranged a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_association" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal association">municipal association</a> with <a href="/wiki/Essingen" class="mw-redirect" title="Essingen">Essingen</a> and <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCttlingen,_Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Hüttlingen, Baden-Württemberg">Hüttlingen</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Council">Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Local_election" title="Local election">local election</a> of 25 May 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council" title="Municipal council">town council</a> consists of 51&#160;representatives having a term of five years. The seats are distributed as follows on parties and groups (changes refer to the second last election of 2004):</p>
