<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayors">Mayors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mayors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1374, the mayor and the council maintain the government of the town. In the 16th century, the town had two, sometimes three mayors, and in 1552, the council had 13 members. Later, the head of the administration was reorganized several times. In the Württemberg era, the mayor's title was initially called <i>Bürgermeister</i>, then from 1819 it was <a href="/wiki/Schulthei%C3%9F" title="Schultheiß">Schultheiß</a>, and since 1947 it is <i>Oberbürgermeister</i>. The mayor is elected for a term of eight years, and he is chairman and a voting member of the council. He has one deputy with the official title of <i>Erster Bürgermeister</i> ("first mayor") and one with the official title of <i>Bürgermeister</i> ("mayor").</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_Flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aalen_Flag.svg/170px-Aalen_Flag.svg.png" width="170" height="476" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aalen_Flag.svg/255px-Aalen_Flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aalen_Flag.svg/340px-Aalen_Flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="1400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalen_Flag.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flag of Aalen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Heads of town in Aalen since 1802</b></p>
<ul>
<li>1802–<span style="visibility:hidden;color:transparent;">0000</span>: Theodor Betzler</li>
<li>1812–1819: Ludwig Hölder</li>
<li>1819–1829: Theodor Betzler</li>
<li>1829:<span style="visibility:hidden;color:transparent;">–0000</span> Palm</li>
<li>1829–1848: Philipp Ehmann</li>
<li>1848–1873: Gustav Oesterlein</li>
<li>1873–1900: Julius Bausch</li>
<li>1900–1902: Paul Maier</li>
<li>1903–1934: Friedrich Schwarz</li>
<li>1935–1945: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Karl_Sch%C3%BCbel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Karl Schübel (page does not exist)">Karl Schübel</a></li>
<li>1945–1950: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Otto_Balluff&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Otto Balluff (page does not exist)">Otto Balluff</a></li>
<li>1950–1975: Karl Schübel</li>
<li>1976–2005: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulrich_Pfeifle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ulrich Pfeifle (page does not exist)">Ulrich Pfeifle</a> (<a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">SPD</a>)</li>
<li>2005–2013: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Gerlach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Martin Gerlach (page does not exist)">Martin Gerlach</a> (independent)</li>
<li>2013-<span style="visibility:hidden;color:transparent;">0000</span>: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thilo_Rentschler&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thilo Rentschler (page does not exist)">Thilo Rentschler</a> (<a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">SPD</a>)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms_and_flag">Coat of arms and flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Coat of arms and flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG/100px-Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG" width="100" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG/150px-Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG/200px-Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1404" data-file-height="1872" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadtwappen_Aalen_1766.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coat of arms of 1766 with eagle and eel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aalen's <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> depicts a black eagle with a red tongue on golden background, having a red shield on its breast with a bent silver <a href="/wiki/Eel" title="Eel">eel</a> on it. Eagle and eel were first acknowledged as Aalen's heraldic animals in the seal of 1385, with the eagle representing the town's <a href="/wiki/Imperial_immediacy" title="Imperial immediacy">imperial immediacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer9_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer9-4">[4]</a></sup> After the territorial reform, it was bestowed again by the <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_(region)" title="Stuttgart (region)">Administrative District of Stuttgart</a> on 16 November 1976.</p>
<p>The coat of arms' <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazon</a> reads: “In gold, the black imperial eagle, with a red breast shield applied to it, therein a bent silver eel” <i>(In Gold der schwarze Reichsadler, belegt mit einem roten Brustschild, darin ein gekrümmter silberner Aal)</i>.</p>
<p>Aalen’s flag is striped in red and white and contains the coat of arms.</p>
<p>The origin of the town’s name is uncertain. <a href="/wiki/Matth%C3%A4us_Merian" title="Matthäus Merian">Matthäus Merian</a> (1593–1650) presumed the name to originate from its location at the Kocher river, where "frequently eels are caught", while <i>Aal</i> is German for "eel". Other explanations point to Aalen as the garrison of an <a href="/wiki/Ala_(Roman_allied_military_unit)" title="Ala (Roman allied military unit)">ala</a> during the Roman empire, respectively to an abridgement of the Roman name "Aquileia" as a potential name of the Roman fort, a name that nearby <a href="/wiki/Heidenheim_an_der_Brenz" title="Heidenheim an der Brenz">Heidenheim an der Brenz</a> bore as well. Another interpretation points to a Celtic word <b>aa</b> meaning "water".<sup id="cite_ref-bauer9_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer9-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twinned_cities">Twinned cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Twinned cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Germany" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany">List of twin towns and sister cities in Germany</a></div>
<p>The "Twin Cities Society of Aalen" <i>(Städtepartnerschaftsverein Aalen e.&#160;V.)</i> promotes "friendly relations" between Aalen and its <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twin cities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> which comprises mutual exchanges of sports and cultural clubs, schools and other civic institutions. On the occasion of the <a href="#Reichsst.C3.A4dter_Tage">Reichsstädter Tage</a>, from 11 until 13 September 2009 the first conference of twinned cities was held.</p>
<p>Aalen has five twin cities:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Saint-L%C3%B4" title="Saint-Lô">Saint-Lô</a> (France), since 1978</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Christchurch,_Dorset" title="Christchurch, Dorset">Christchurch</a> (United Kingdom), since 1981</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary"><img alt="Hungary" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tatab%C3%A1nya" title="Tatabánya">Tatabánya</a> (Hungary), since 1987</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey"><img alt="Turkey" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Antakya" title="Antakya">Antakya</a> (Turkey), since 1995. This twinning arrangement was initiated by Ismail Demirtas, who emigrated in 1962 from Turkey to Aalen and was social adviser for foreign employees.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy"><img alt="Italy" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Cervia" title="Cervia">Cervia</a> (Italy), since 2011</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Godparenthood">Godparenthood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Godparenthood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the occasion of the 1980 <i>Reichsstädter Tage</i>, Aalen took over godparenthood for the more than 3000 ethnic Germans displaced from the <a href="/wiki/Vy%C5%A1kov" title="Vyškov">Wischau</a> linguistic enclave. 972 of them settled in Aalen in 1946. The "Wischau Linguistic Enclave Society" <i>(Gemeinschaft Wischauer Sprachinsel)</i> regularly organises commemorative meetings in Aalen. Their traditional costumes are stored in the <a href="#Old_Town_Hall">Old Town Hall</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_finances">Municipal finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Municipal finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the 2007 municipal poll by the Baden-Württemberg chapter of the <a href="/wiki/German_Taxpayers_Federation" title="German Taxpayers Federation">German Taxpayers Federation</a>, municipal tax revenues totalling to 54,755 million Euros (2006) resp. 62,148 million Euros (2007) face the following debts:<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<ul>
<li>2006 total: 109.9 million Euros debts (64.639 millions of the finance department and 48.508 millions of the municipal enterprises and fund assets)</li>
<li>2007 total: 114.5 million Euros debts (69.448 millions of the finance department and 45.052 millions of the municipal enterprises and fund assets)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_sights">Culture and sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culture and sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The town operates the “Theatre of the Town of Aalen” <i>(Theater der Stadt Aalen)</i>. Having been founded in 1991 and featuring six salaried actors, it is the newest as well as the smallest civic theatre in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In addition to regular plays, it also offers four theatre clubs for all age levels. During the 2008/2009 season, 400 performances of ten productions attracted more than 21,000 visitors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schubart_Literary_Award">Schubart Literary Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Schubart Literary Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The town endowed the "Schubart Literary Award" <i>(Schubart-Literaturpreis)</i> in 1955 in tribute to <a href="/wiki/Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart" title="Christian Friedrich Daniel Schubart">Christian Friedrich Daniel Schubart</a>, who spent his childhood and youth in Aalen. It is one of the earliest literary awards in Baden-Württemberg and is awarded biennially to German-language writers whose work coincide with Schubart's "liberal and enlightened reasoning".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> It is compensated with 12,000&#160;Euros.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Founded in 1958, the "<a href="/wiki/Music_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Music School">Music School</a> of the Town of Aalen" today has about 1,500 students taught by 27 music instructors in 30 subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In 1977, a <a href="/wiki/Symphony_orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Symphony orchestra">symphony orchestra</a> was founde in Aalen, which today is called <i>Aalener Sinfonieorchester</i>, and consists mostly of instructors and students of the music school. It performs three public concerts annually: The “New Year’s Concert” in January, the “Symphony Concert” in July and a “Christmas Concert” in December.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Beyond that, music festivals regularly take place in Aalen, like the <a href="/wiki/Aalen_Jazzfest" class="mw-redirect" title="Aalen Jazzfest">Aalen Jazzfest</a>.</p>
<p>The Aalen volunteer fire department has had a <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a> since 1952, whose roots date back to 1883. In 1959, the band received its first <a href="/wiki/Glockenspiel" title="Glockenspiel">glockenspiel</a> from TV host <a href="/wiki/Peter_Frankenfeld" title="Peter Frankenfeld">Peter Frankenfeld</a> on the occasion of a TV appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>A famous German rapper, designer and singer, that goes under the name of Cro, was born in Aalen and lived his early years here.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_memorial_sites">Museums and memorial sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Museums and memorial sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg/220px-Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg/330px-Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg/440px-Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Limesmuseum_Aalen_Aussenansicht.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aalen Limes Museum, exterior view</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the central district of Aalen, there are two museums: The “Aalen <a href="/wiki/Limes_Germanicus" title="Limes Germanicus">Limes</a> Museum" <i>(Limesmuseum Aalen)</i> is located at the place of the largest <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">Roman cavalry fort</a> north of the Alps until about 200 AD. It opened in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-54">[54]</a></sup> The museum exhibits numerous objects from the Roman era. The ruins of the cavalry fort located beside the museum is open to museum visitors. Every other year, a Roman festival is held in the area of the museum (<a href="#Roman_Festival">see below</a>).</p>
<p>In the Geological-Paleontological Museum located in the historic town hall, there are more than 1500 fossils from the Swabian Jura, including <a href="/wiki/Ammonite" class="mw-redirect" title="Ammonite">ammonites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ichthyosaur" title="Ichthyosaur">ichthyosaurs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">corals</a>, displayed.</p>
<p>In the Waldhausen district the <i>Heimatstüble</i> museum of local history has an exhibition on agriculture and rural living.</p>
<p>In the Wasseralfingen district, there are two more museums: The <i>Museum Wasseralfingen</i> comprises a local history exhibition and an art gallery including works of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hermann_Plock&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hermann Plock (page does not exist)">Hermann Plock</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Helmut_Schuster&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Helmut Schuster (page does not exist)">Helmut Schuster</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sieger_K%C3%B6der&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sieger Köder (page does not exist)">Sieger Köder</a>. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Stove" title="Stove">stove</a> plate collection of the <i>Schwäbische Hüttenwerke</i> steel mill is exhibited, with artists, modellers and the production sequence of a cast plate from design to final product being presented.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorial_sites">Memorial sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Memorial sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg/170px-Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg/255px-Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg/340px-Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gedenkstein_Schillerlinde_Wasseralfingen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial stone at <i>Schillerlinde</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There is memorial stone at the <i>Schillerlinde</i> tree above Wasseralfingen's ore pit dedicated to four prisoners of the subcamp of Natzweiler-Struthof concentration camp killed there. Also in Wasseralfingen, in the cemetery a memorial with the Polish inscription "To the victims of Hitler" which commemorates the deceased forced labourers buried there.<sup id="cite_ref-gedenkstaetten_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gedenkstaetten-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1954, on the <i>Schillerhöhe</i> hill the town erected a bell tower as a memorial to Aalen's victims of both world wars and to the <a href="/wiki/Heimatvertriebene" title="Heimatvertriebene">displacement of ethnic Germans</a>. The tower was planned by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Emil_Leo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Emil Leo (page does not exist)">Emil Leo</a>, the bell was endowed by Carl Schneider. The tower is open on request. Every evening at 18:45 (before 2003: at 19:45), the memorial's bell rings.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buildings">Buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches">Churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg/220px-Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg/330px-Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg/440px-Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1654" data-file-height="1238" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johanneskirche_Aalen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
St. John's Church</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Stephanus,_Wasseralfingen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/St._Stephanus%2C_Wasseralfingen.jpg/170px-St._Stephanus%2C_Wasseralfingen.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/St._Stephanus%2C_Wasseralfingen.jpg/255px-St._Stephanus%2C_Wasseralfingen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/St._Stephanus%2C_Wasseralfingen.jpg/340px-St._Stephanus%2C_Wasseralfingen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Stephanus,_Wasseralfingen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
St. Stephen's Church, Wasseralfingen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The town centre is dominated by the Evangelical-Lutheran <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">St. Nicholas'</a> Church in the heart of the pedestrian area. The church, in its present shape being built between 1765 and 1767, is the only major <a href="/wiki/Late_Baroque" class="mw-redirect" title="Late Baroque">Late Baroque</a> building in Aalen and is the main church of the Evangelical-Lutheran parish of Aalen.</p>
<p><i>St. John's Church</i> is located inside of St. John's cemetery in the western centre. The building presumably is from the 9th century and thus is one of Württemberg's oldest existing churches. The interior features <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">frescos</a> from the early 13th century.</p>
<p>For other churches in Aalen, see the <a href="#Religions">Religions</a> section.</p>
<h4><span id="Historic_Town_Hall_with_&quot;Spy&quot;"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_Town_Hall_with_.22Spy.22">Historic Town Hall with "Spy"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Historic Town Hall with &quot;Spy&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spionturm_Aalen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Spionturm_Aalen.jpg/170px-Spionturm_Aalen.jpg" width="170" height="348" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Spionturm_Aalen.jpg/255px-Spionturm_Aalen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Spionturm_Aalen.jpg/340px-Spionturm_Aalen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="679" data-file-height="1390" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spionturm_Aalen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Spy's Tower"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Historic Town Hall was originally built in the 14th century. After the fire of 1634, it was re-constructed in 1636. This building received a clock from Lauterburg,<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> and the Imperial City of <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> donated a <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">Carillon</a>. It features a figurine of the "Spy of Aalen" and historically displayed other figurines, however the latter ones were lost by a fire in 1884. Since then, the Spy resides inside the reconstructed tower and has become a symbol of the town. The building was used as the town hall until 1907. Since 1977, the Geological-Paleontological Museum resides in the Historic Town Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-Citybummel_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citybummel-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to legend, the citizens of Aalen owe the "Spy of Aalen" <i>(Spion von Aalen)</i> their town having been spared from destruction by the emperor's army:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The Imperial City of Aalen once was were in quarrel with the emperor, and his army was shortly before the gates to take the town. The people of Aalen got scared and thus dispatched their “most cunning” one out into the enemy’s camp to spy out the strength of their troops. Without any digression, he went straight into the middle of the enemy camp, which inescapably led to him being seized and presented to the emperor. When the emperor asked him what he had lost here, he answered in <a href="/wiki/Swabian_German" title="Swabian German">Swabian German</a>: "Don't frighten, high lords, I just want to peek how many cannons and other war things you've got, since I am the spy of Aalen". The emperor laughed upon such a blatancy and <i>acted</i> naïvety, steered him all through the camp and then sent him back home. Soon the emperor withdrew with his army as he thought a town such <i>wise guys</i> reside in deserved being spared.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Town_Hall">Old Town Hall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Old Town Hall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The earliest record of the Old Town Hall was in 1575. Its outside wall features the oldest known coat of arms, which is of 1664. Until 1851, the building also housed the <i>Krone-Post</i> hotel, which coincided with being a station of the <a href="/wiki/Thurn-und-Taxis-Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Thurn-und-Taxis-Post">Thurn und Taxis postal company</a>. It has housed many notable persons. Thus the so-called "Napoleon Window" with its "N" painted on reminds of the stay of French emperor <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> in 1805. According to legend, he rammed his head so hard it bled on this window, when he was startled by the noise of his soldiers ridiculing the "Spy of Aalen".<sup id="cite_ref-bauer145_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer145-29">[29]</a></sup> The building was used as Aalen's town hall from 1907 until 1975. Today it houses a cabaret café and the stage of the Theatre of the Town of Aalen. The town has adopted the <i>Wischau Linguistic Enclave Society</i> due to their godparenthood and stores their traditional constumes in the building.</p>
<h4><span id="Bürgerspital"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="B.C3.BCrgerspital">Bürgerspital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Bürgerspital">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i>Bürgerspital</i> ("Civic Asylum") is a <a href="/wiki/Timber_framing" title="Timber framing">timber-frame</a> house erected on <i>Spritzenhausplatz</i> ("Fire Engine House Square") in 1702. Until 1873, it was used as civic hospital, then, later as a retirement home. After a comprehensive renovation in 1980 it was turned into a senior citizen's community centre.<sup id="cite_ref-Citybummel_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citybummel-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Limes-Thermen">Limes-Thermen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Limes-Thermen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On a slope of the <i>Langert</i> mountain, south of the town, the <i>Limes-Thermen</i> ("Limes <a href="/wiki/Thermae" title="Thermae">Thermae</a>") <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">hot springs</a> are located. They were built in ancient Roman style and opened in 1985. The health spa is supplied with water about 34 to 36&#160;°C (93 to 97&#160;°F).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Market_square">Market square</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Market square">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The market square is the historic hub of Aalen and runs along about 150 metres (490&#160;ft) from the town hall in the south to the Historic Town Hall and the Old Town Hall in the north, where it empties into <i>Radgasse</i> alley. Since 1809, it is site of the weekly market on Wednesday and Saturday. About 10 metres (33&#160;ft) in front of the <i>Reichsstädter Brunnen</i> fountain at the town hall, the coats of arms of Aalen, its twinned cities and of the Wischau linguistic enclave are paved into the street as mosaic.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Market_fountain">Market fountain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Market fountain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg/220px-Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg/330px-Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg/440px-Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marktbrunnen_Aalen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue depicting <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph I, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph&#160;I</a> at the market fountain</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1705, for the water supply of Aalen a well casing was erected at the northern point of the market square, in front of the Historic Town Hall. It was a present of duke <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_Louis,_Duke_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Eberhard Louis, Duke of Württemberg">Eberhard Louis</a>. The fountain bore a statue of emperor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph I, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph&#160;I.</a>, who was enthroned in 1705 and in 1707 renewed Aalen's Imperial City privileges.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer82_24-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer82-24">[24]</a></sup> The fountain was supplied via a wooden pipe. Excessive water was dissipated through ditches branched from Kocher river. When in the early 1870s Aalen's water network was constructed, the fountain was replaced by a smaller fountain about 100 metres (330&#160;ft) distant. In 1975, the old market fountain was re-erected in baroque style. It bears a replica of the emperor's statue, with the original statue exhibited in the new town hall's lobby. The <a href="/wiki/Cast_iron" title="Cast iron">cast iron</a> casing plates depict the 1718 coat of arms of the Duchy of Württemberg and the coats of arms of Aalen and of the merged municipalities.</p>
<h5><span id="Reichsstädter_Brunnen"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Reichsst.C3.A4dter_Brunnen">Reichsstädter Brunnen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Reichsstädter Brunnen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <i>Reichsstädter Brunnen</i> fountain ("Imperial Civic Fountain") is located in front of the town hall at the southern point of the market square. It was created by sculptor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fritz_Nuss&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fritz Nuss (page does not exist)">Fritz Nuss</a> in 1977 to commemorate Aalen's time as an Imperial City (1360–1803). On its circumference is a <a href="/wiki/Frieze" title="Frieze">frieze</a> showing bronze figurines illustrating the town's history.<sup id="cite_ref-Citybummel_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citybummel-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Radgasse">Radgasse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Radgasse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i>Radgasse</i> ("Wheel Alley") features Aalen's oldest façade. Originally a small pond was on its side. The buildings were erected between 1659 and 1662 for peasants with citizenry privileges and renovated in the mid-1980s. The namesake for the alley was the "Wheel" tavern, which was to be found at the site of today's address <i>Radgasse 15</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Citybummel_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citybummel-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tiefer_Stollen">Tiefer Stollen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Tiefer Stollen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG/220px-Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG/330px-Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG/440px-Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eingang_Besucherbergwerk_Tiefer_Stollen_heute.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Tiefer Stollen</i> tourist mine</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The former iron ore pit <i>Wilhelm</i> at Braunenberg hill was converted into the <i>Tiefer Stollen</i> tourist mine in order to remind of the old-day miners' efforts and to maintain it as a memorial of early industrialisation in the Aalen area. It has a mining museum open for visitors, and a <a href="/wiki/Mine_railway" title="Mine railway">mine railway</a> takes visitors deep into the mountain. The Town of Aalen, a sponsorship association, and many citizens volunteered several thousand hours of labour to put the mine into its current state. As far as possible, things were left in the original state. In 1989, a sanitary gallery was established where respiratory diseases are treated within rest cures.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Thus the Aalen village of Röthard, where the gallery is located, was awarded the title of "Place with sanitary gallery service" in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Observatory">Observatory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Observatory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Aalen Observatory was built in 1969 as school observatory for the Schubart <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">Gymnasium</a>. In 2001, it was converted to a public observatory. Since then, it has been managed by the <i>Astronomische Arbeitsgemeinschaft Aalen</i> ("Aalen Astronomical Society"). It is located on Schillerhöhe hill and features two <a href="/wiki/Refractive_telescope" class="mw-redirect" title="Refractive telescope">refractive telescopes</a>. They were manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Zeiss_AG" title="Carl Zeiss AG">Carl Zeiss AG</a> which has its headquarters in nearby Oberkochen and operates a manufacturing works in Aalen (<a href="#Economy_and_infrastructure">see below</a>). In the observatory, guided tours and lectures are held regularly.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Windpark_Waldhausen">Windpark Waldhausen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Windpark Waldhausen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG/220px-Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG/330px-Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG/440px-Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Windrad_Waldhausen_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wind turbine at Windpark Waldhausen</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Windpark Waldhausen</i> <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farm</a> began operations in early 2007. It consists of seven <a href="/wiki/REpower" class="mw-redirect" title="REpower">REpower</a> MM92 wind turbines with a <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">nameplate capacity</a> of 2 MW each.<sup id="cite_ref-windpark_waldhausen_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-windpark_waldhausen-59">[59]</a></sup> The hub height of each wind turbine is 100 metres (330&#160;ft), with a rotor diameter of 92 metres (302&#160;ft).</p>
<h4><span id="Aalbäumle_observation_tower"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Aalb.C3.A4umle_observation_tower">Aalbäumle observation tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Aalbäumle observation tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg/170px-Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg/255px-Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg/340px-Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2247" data-file-height="3029" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aalb%C3%A4umle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Aalbäumle</i> observation tower</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 26 metres (85&#160;ft) tall <i>Aalbäumle</i> observation tower is built atop <i>Langert</i> mountain. This popular hiking destination was built in 1898 and was remodelled in 1992. It features a good view over Aalen and the Welland region, up to the Rosenstein mountain and Ellwangen. Beneath the tower, an adventure playground and a cabin is located. A flag on the tower signals whether the cabin's restaurant is open.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_monuments">Natural monuments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Natural monuments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Baden-Württemberg State Institute for Environment, Measurements and Natural Conservation has laid out six protected landscapes in Aalen (the <i>Swabian Jura escarpment between Lautern and Aalen with adjacent territories</i>, the <i>Swabian Jura escarpment between Unterkochen and Baiershofen</i>, the <i>Hilllands around Hofen</i>, the <i>Kugeltal and Ebnater Tal valleys with parts of Heiligental valley and adjacent territories</i>, <i>Laubachtal valley</i> and <i>Lower Lein Valley with side valleys</i>), two sanctuary forests (<i>Glashütte</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kocher" title="Kocher">Kocher</a> Origin</i>), 65 extensive <a href="/wiki/Natural_monument" title="Natural monument">natural monuments</a>, 30 individual natural monuments and the following two <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas">protected areas</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 24.1 hectares (60 acres) large <i>Dellenhäule</i> protected area between Aalen's Waldhausen district and Neresheim's Elchingen district, created in 1969, is a sheep pasture with <a href="/wiki/Juniper" title="Juniper">juniper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wood_pasture" title="Wood pasture">wood pasture</a> of old willow oaks.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 46.5 hectares (115 acres) large <i>Goldshöfer Sande</i> protected area was established in 2000 and is situated between Aalen's Hofen district and Hüttlingen. The sands on the hill originated from the <a href="/wiki/Early_Pleistocene" title="Early Pleistocene">Early Pleistocene</a> are of geological importance, and the various grove structures offer habitat to severely endangered bird species.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WaldstadionAalen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/WaldstadionAalen.jpg/330px-WaldstadionAalen.jpg" width="330" height="87" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/WaldstadionAalen.jpg/495px-WaldstadionAalen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/WaldstadionAalen.jpg/660px-WaldstadionAalen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1648" data-file-height="432" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WaldstadionAalen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Scholz Arena</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The football team, <a href="/wiki/VfR_Aalen" title="VfR Aalen">VfR Aalen</a>, was founded in 1921 and played in the <a href="/wiki/2._Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="2. Fußball-Bundesliga">2nd German League</a> between 2012 and 2015, after which they were relegated to <a href="/wiki/3._Liga" title="3. Liga">3. Liga</a>. Its playing venue is the <a href="/wiki/Scholz-Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Scholz-Arena">Scholz-Arena</a> situated in the west of the town, which bore the name <i>Städtisches Waldstadion Aalen</i> ("Civic Forest Stadium of Aalen") until 2008. From 1939 until 1945, the VfR played in the <a href="/wiki/Gauliga_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Gauliga Württemberg">Gauliga Württemberg</a>, then one of several parallel top-ranking soccer leagues of Germany.</p>
<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=KSV_Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="KSV Aalen (page does not exist)">KSV Aalen</a> wrestles in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(wrestling)" title="Bundesliga (wrestling)">Wrestling Federal League</a>. It was German champion in team wrestling in 2010. Its predecessor, the <i>KSV Germania Aalen</i> disbanded in 2005, was German champion eight times and runner-up five times since 1976. Another Aalen club, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=TSV_Dewangen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="TSV Dewangen (page does not exist)">TSV Dewangen</a>, wrestled in the Federal League until 2009.</p>
<p>Two American sports, <a href="/wiki/American_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="American Football">American Football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">Baseball</a>, are pursued by the <i>MTV Aalen</i>. <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">Volleyball</a> has been gaining in popularity in Aalen for years. The first men's team of <i>DJK Aalen</i> accomplished qualification for regional league in the season of 2008/09.</p>
<p>The <i>Ostalb</i> ski lifts are located south of the town centre, at the northern slope of the Swabian Jura. The skiing area comprises two <a href="/wiki/Platter_lift" class="mw-redirect" title="Platter lift">platter lifts</a> that have a vertical rise of 130 and 30 metres (427 and 98&#160;ft), with two runs with lengths of 800 and 1,200 metres (2,600 and 3,900&#160;ft) and a beginners' run.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regular_events">Regular events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Regular events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Reichsstädter_Tage"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Reichsst.C3.A4dter_Tage">Reichsstädter Tage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Reichsstädter Tage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since 1975, <i>Reichsstädter Tage</i> ("Imperial City days") festival is held annually in the town centre on the second weekend in September. It is deemed the largest festival of the <a href="/wiki/Ostw%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Ostwürttemberg">Ostwürttemberg</a> region,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> and is associated with a shopping Sunday in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Ladenschlussgesetz" title="Ladenschlussgesetz">Ladenschlussgesetz</a> code. The festival is also attended by delegations from the twinned cities. On the town hall square, on Sunday an <a href="/wiki/Ecumenism" title="Ecumenism">ecumenical service</a> is held.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Festival">Roman Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Roman Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The international Roman Festival <i>(Römertage)</i> are held biannially on the site of the former Roman fort and the modern Limes museum. The festival's ninth event in 2008 was attended by around 11,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aalen_Jazz_Festival">Aalen Jazz Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Aalen Jazz Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Annually during the second week of November, the <a href="/wiki/Aalen_Jazz_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Aalen Jazz Festival">Aalen Jazz Festival</a> brings known and unknown artists to Aalen. It has already featured musicians like <a href="/wiki/Miles_Davis" title="Miles Davis">Miles Davis</a>, <a href="/wiki/B._B._King" class="mw-redirect" title="B. B. King">B. B. King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Charles" title="Ray Charles">Ray Charles</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Murray_(saxophonist)" title="David Murray (saxophonist)">David Murray</a>, <a href="/wiki/McCoy_Tyner" title="McCoy Tyner">McCoy Tyner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Jarreau" title="Al Jarreau">Al Jarreau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esbj%C3%B6rn_Svensson" title="Esbjörn Svensson">Esbjörn Svensson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Mangelsdorff" title="Albert Mangelsdorff">Albert Mangelsdorff</a>. The festival is complemented by individual concerts in spring and summer, and, including the individual concerts, comprises around 25 concerts with a total of about 13,000 visitors.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2008 there were 30,008 employees liable to <a href="/wiki/Social_insurance" title="Social insurance">social insurance</a> living in Aalen. 13,946 (46.5&#160;percent) were employed in the <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">manufacturing sector</a>, 4,715 (15.7&#160;percent) in commerce, catering, hotels and transport, and 11,306 (37.7&#160;percent) in other services.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Annually 16,000 employees commute to work, with about 9,000 living in the town and commuting out.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Altogether in Aalen there are about 4,700 business enterprises, 1,100 of them being registered in the <a href="/wiki/German_Trade_Register" title="German Trade Register">trade register</a>. The others comprise 2,865 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kleingewerbe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kleingewerbe (page does not exist)">small enterprises</a> and 701 craft enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-Unternehmen_und_Betriebe_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unternehmen_und_Betriebe-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Aalen, <a href="/wiki/Metalworking" title="Metalworking">metalworking</a> is the predominant industry, along with machine-building. Other industries include <a href="/wiki/Optics" title="Optics">optics</a>, paper, information technology, <a href="/wiki/Chemicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemicals">chemicals</a>, textiles,<sup id="cite_ref-EB_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-54">[54]</a></sup> medical instruments, pharmaceuticals, and food.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohen_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable enterprises include <i>SHW Automotive</i> (originating from the former <i>Schwäbische Hüttenwerke</i> steel mills and a mill of 1671 in Wasseralfingen), the <i>Alfing Kessler</i> engineering works, the precision tools manufacturer <i>MAPAL Dr.&#160;Kress</i>, the snow chain manufacturer <i>RUD&#160;Ketten&#160;Rieger&#160;&amp;&#160;Dietz</i> and its subsidiary <i>Erlau</i>, the <i>Gesenkschmiede Schneider</i> forging die smithery, the <i>SDZ Druck und Medien</i> media company, the <i>Papierfabrik Palm</i> paper mill, the alarm system manufacturer <i>Telenot</i>, the laser show provider <i>LOBO electronic</i> and the <a href="/wiki/Finishing_(textiles)" title="Finishing (textiles)">textile finisher</a> <i>Lindenfarb</i>, which all have their seat in Aalen. A branch in Aalen is maintained by optical systems manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Carl_Zeiss_AG" title="Carl Zeiss AG">Carl Zeiss</a> headquartered in nearby Oberkochen.<sup id="cite_ref-Unternehmen_und_Betriebe_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unternehmen_und_Betriebe-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg/220px-Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg/330px-Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg/440px-Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="999" data-file-height="580" /></a>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahnhof_Aalen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aalen station</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Aalen_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Aalen station">Aalen station</a> is a regional railway hub on the <a href="/wiki/Rems_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Rems Railway">Rems Railway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Hauptbahnhof" title="Stuttgart Hauptbahnhof">Stuttgart</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brenz_Railway" title="Brenz Railway">Brenz Railway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ulm_Hauptbahnhof" title="Ulm Hauptbahnhof">Ulm</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Jagst_Railway" title="Upper Jagst Railway">Upper Jagst Railway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Crailsheim" title="Crailsheim">Crailsheim</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ries_Railway" title="Ries Railway">Ries Railway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Donauw%C3%B6rth_station" title="Donauwörth station">Donauwörth</a>. Until 1972, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=H%C3%A4rtsfeld_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Härtsfeld Railway (page does not exist)">Härtsfeld Railway</a> connected Aalen with <a href="/wiki/Dillingen_an_der_Donau" title="Dillingen an der Donau">Dillingen an der Donau</a> via <a href="/wiki/Neresheim" title="Neresheim">Neresheim</a>. Other railway stations within the town limits are <i>Hofen (b Aalen)</i>, <i>Unterkochen</i>, <i>Wasseralfingen</i> and <a href="/wiki/Goldsh%C3%B6fe_station" title="Goldshöfe station">Goldshöfe station</a>. The <i>Aalen-Erlau</i> stop situated in the south is no longer operational.</p>
<p>Aalen station is served at two-hour intervals by trains of <a href="/wiki/Intercity_(Deutsche_Bahn)" title="Intercity (Deutsche Bahn)">Intercity</a> line 61 <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Hauptbahnhof" title="Karlsruhe Hauptbahnhof">Karlsruhe</a>–Stuttgart–Aalen–<a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hauptbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hauptbahnhof">Nuremberg</a>. For regional rail travel, Aalen is served by various lines of the <a href="/wiki/Interregio-Express" title="Interregio-Express">Interregio-Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regional-Express" title="Regional-Express">Regional-Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regionalbahn" title="Regionalbahn">Regionalbahn</a> categories. The town also operates the Aalen <a href="/wiki/Industrial_railway" title="Industrial railway">industrial railway</a> <i>(Industriebahn Aalen)</i>, which carries about 250 carloads per year.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Street">Street</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Street">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The junctions of <i>Aalen/<a href="/wiki/Westhausen_(Ostalb)" title="Westhausen (Ostalb)">Westhausen</a></i> and <i>Aalen/Oberkochen</i> connect Aalen with the <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_7" title="Bundesautobahn 7">A7</a> (<a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>–<a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCssen" title="Füssen">Füssen</a>). Federal roads (<i><a href="/wiki/Bundesstra%C3%9Fe" title="Bundesstraße">Bundesstraßen</a></i>) connecting with Aalen are <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_19&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bundesstraße 19 (page does not exist)">B&#160;19</a> (<a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>–<a href="/wiki/Ulm" title="Ulm">Ulm</a>), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_29&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bundesstraße 29 (page does not exist)">B&#160;29</a> (<a href="/wiki/Waiblingen" title="Waiblingen">Waiblingen</a>–<a href="/wiki/N%C3%B6rdlingen" title="Nördlingen">Nördlingen</a>) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bundesstra%C3%9Fe_290&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bundesstraße 290 (page does not exist)">B&#160;290</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tauberbischofsheim" title="Tauberbischofsheim">Tauberbischofsheim</a>–Westhausen). The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Schw%C3%A4bische_Dichterstra%C3%9Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Schwäbische Dichterstraße (page does not exist)">Schwäbische Dichterstraße</a> ("Swabian Poets' Route") tourist route established in 1977/78 leads through Aalen.</p>
<p>Several bus lines operate within the borough. The <i>Omnibus-Verkehr Aalen</i> company is one of the few in Germany that use <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double-decker buses</a>, it has done so since 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> A district-wide fare system, <i>OstalbMobil</i>, has been in effect since 2007.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Stuttgart Airport, offering international connections, is about 90 kilometres (56&#160;mi) away, the travel time by train is about 100&#160;Minutes. At <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen-Heidenheim_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aalen-Heidenheim Airport (page does not exist)">Aalen-Heidenheim Airport</a>, located 15 kilometres (9.3&#160;mi) south-east of Aalen, small aircraft are permitted. <a href="/wiki/Gliding" title="Gliding">Gliding</a> airfields nearby are in <a href="/wiki/Heubach" title="Heubach">Heubach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bartholom%C3%A4" title="Bartholomä">Bartholomä</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle">Bicycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Bicycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bicycle routes stretching through Aalen are the <i>Deutscher Limes-Radweg</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Limes_Germanicus" title="Limes Germanicus">German Limes</a> Bicycle Route") and the <i>Kocher-Jagst</i> Bicycle Route.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_facilities">Public facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Public facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aalen houses an <a href="/wiki/Amtsgericht" title="Amtsgericht">Amtsgericht</a> (local district court), chambers of the Stuttgart <a href="/wiki/Labor_court" title="Labor court">Labour Court</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_notary" title="Civil law notary">notary's office</a>, a tax office and an <a href="/wiki/Employment_agency" title="Employment agency">employment agency</a>. It is the seat of the Ostalbkreis district office, of the Aalen Deanery of the Evangelical-Lutheran Church and of the <i>Ostalb</i> deanery of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Rottenburg-Stuttgart" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Rottenburg-Stuttgart">Roman Catholic Diocese of Rottenburg-Stuttgart</a>.</p>
<p>The Stuttgart <a href="/wiki/Administrative_court" title="Administrative court">administrative court</a>, the Stuttgart Labour Court and the Ulm Social Welfare Court are in charge for Aalen.</p>
<p>Aalen had a civic hospital, which resided in the <i>Bürgerspital</i> building until 1873, then in a building at <i>Alte Heidenheimer Straße</i>. In 1942, the hospital was taken over by the district. The district hospital at the present site of <i>Kälblesrain</i>, known today as <i>Ostalb-Klinikum</i>, was opened in 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer145_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer145-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first local newspaper, <i>Der Bote von Aalen</i> ("The Herald of Aalen"), has been published on Wednesdays and Saturdays since 1837.<sup id="cite_ref-bauer145_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauer145-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Currently, local newspapers published in Aalen are the <i><a href="/wiki/Schw%C3%A4bische_Post" title="Schwäbische Post">Schwäbische Post</a></i>, which obtains its supra-regional pages from the Ulm-based <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCdwestpresse" class="mw-redirect" title="Südwestpresse">Südwestpresse</a>, and the <i>Aalener Nachrichten</i> (erstwhile <i>Aalener Volkszeitung</i>), a local edition of <a href="/wiki/Schw%C3%A4bische_Zeitung" title="Schwäbische Zeitung">Schwäbische Zeitung</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leutkirch_im_Allg%C3%A4u" title="Leutkirch im Allgäu">Leutkirch im Allgäu</a>.</p>
<p>Two of Germany's biggest <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesezirkel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lesezirkel (page does not exist)">Lesezirkels</a> (magazine rental services) are headquartered in Aalen: <i>Brabandt LZ Plus Media</i> and <i>Lesezirkel Portal</i>.</p>
<p>Regional event magazines are <i>Xaver</i>, <i>åla</i>, <i>ålakultur</i>.</p>
<p>The commercial broadcasters <i>Radio Ton</i> and <i>Radio 7</i> have studios in Aalen.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Latin_school" title="Latin school">Latin school</a> was first recorded in Aalen in 1447; it was remodeled in 1616 and also later in various buildings that were all situated near the town church, and continued up through the 19th century. In the course of the reformation, a "German school" was established in tandem, being a predecessor of the latter <a href="/wiki/Volksschule" title="Volksschule">Volksschule</a> school type. In 1860, the <i>Ritterschule</i> was built as a <i>Volksschule</i> for girls; the building today houses the <i>Pestalozzischule</i>. In 1866, a new building was erected for the Latin school and for the <a href="/wiki/Realschule" title="Realschule">Realschule</a> established in 1840. This building, later known as the <i>Alte Gewerbeschule</i>, was torn down in 1975 to free up land for the new town hall. In 1912, the <i>Parkschule</i> building was opened. It was designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bonatz" title="Paul Bonatz">Paul Bonatz</a> and today houses the <i>Schubart-<a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">Gymnasium</a></i></p>
<p>The biggest educational institution in the town is the <i><a href="/wiki/Hochschule" title="Hochschule">Hochschule</a> Aalen</i>, which was founded in 1962 and focuses on engineering and economics. It is attended by 5000 students on five campuses and employs 129 professors and 130 other lecturers.</p>
<p>The town provides three <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">Gymnasiums</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Realschule" title="Realschule">Realschulen</a>, two <i>Förderschulen</i> (<a href="/wiki/Special_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Special school">special schools</a>), six combined <a href="/wiki/Grundschule" class="mw-redirect" title="Grundschule">Grundschulen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hauptschule" title="Hauptschule">Hauptschulen</a> and eight standalone Grundschulen. The Ostalbkreis district provides three vocational schools and three additional special schools. Finally, six non-state schools of various types exist.</p>
<p>The German <a href="/wiki/Esperanto" title="Esperanto">Esperanto</a> Library (German: <i>Deutsche Esperanto-Bibliothek</i>, Esperanto: <i>Germana Esperanto-Biblioteko</i>) has been located in the building of the town library since 1989.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TV_and_radio_transmission_tower">TV and radio transmission tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: TV and radio transmission tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCdwestrundfunk" title="Südwestrundfunk">Südwestrundfunk</a> broadcasting company operates the Aalen <a href="/wiki/Transmitter" title="Transmitter">transmission tower</a> on the <i>Braunenberg</i> hill. The tower was erected in 1956, it is 140 metres (460&#160;ft) tall and made of <a href="/wiki/Reinforced_concrete" title="Reinforced concrete">reinforced concrete</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Things_named_after_Aalen">Things named after Aalen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Things named after Aalen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following vehicles are named "Aalen":</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-500" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-500">Boeing 737-500</a> <i>D-ABJF</i></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> <a href="/wiki/ICE_3" title="ICE 3">ICE 3</a> <i>Tz309</i> (since 2 June 2008)<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Persons_connected_to_Aalen">Persons connected to Aalen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Persons connected to Aalen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honorary_citizens">Honorary citizens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Honorary citizens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Ruland Ayßlinger, composer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Erwin Rommel</a> (1891–1944), Field Marshal of World War II, grew up in Aalen</li>
<li>Paul Edel<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li>Wilhelm Jakob Schweiker (1859–1927), founder of the Aalen Historical Society <i>(Geschichts- und Altertumsverein Aalen</i>) and name giver of the Wilhelm Jakob Schweiker Award<sup id="cite_ref-GA_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulrich_Pfeifle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ulrich Pfeifle (page does not exist)">Ulrich Pfeifle</a>, Mayor of Aalen from 1976 until 2005</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Persons_born_in_Aalen">Persons born in Aalen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Persons born in Aalen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_(GPh43).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_%28GPh43%29.jpg/150px-P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_%28GPh43%29.jpg" width="150" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_%28GPh43%29.jpg/225px-P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_%28GPh43%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_%28GPh43%29.jpg/300px-P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_%28GPh43%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="626" data-file-height="863" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:P_Sinner_-_Bischof_Karl_Joseph_Hefele_1869_(GPh43).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Karl Joseph von Hefele 1869</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Christoph_von_Westerstetten" title="Johann Christoph von Westerstetten">Johann Christoph von Westerstetten</a> (1563-1637), Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Eichstaett" class="mw-redirect" title="Eichstaett">Eichstaett</a> and counter-reformer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_Joseph_von_Hefele" class="mw-redirect" title="Karl Joseph von Hefele">Karl Joseph von Hefele</a> (1809–1893), Roman Catholic theologian, clerical historian and bishop</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_Wahl" title="Karl Wahl">Karl Wahl</a> (1892-1981), Gauleiter of Swabia, <a href="/wiki/Obergruppenf%C3%BChrer" title="Obergruppenführer">Obergruppenführer</a></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kurt_Jooss.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Kurt_Jooss.jpg/150px-Kurt_Jooss.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Kurt_Jooss.jpg/225px-Kurt_Jooss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Kurt_Jooss.jpg/300px-Kurt_Jooss.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1243" data-file-height="1657" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kurt_Jooss.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kurt Jooss 1971</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kurt_Jooss" title="Kurt Jooss">Kurt Jooss</a> (1901-1979), born in Wasseralfingen; dancer, choreographer and dance educator</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/August_Zehender" title="August Zehender">August Zehender</a> (1903-1945), SS Brigade Commander and Major General of the Waffen-SS</li>
<li>Paul Buck (1911-2006), piano teacher</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruno_Heck" title="Bruno Heck">Bruno Heck</a> (1917–1989), politician of the CDU, former minister of the federal government and CDU secretary general</li>
<li>Alfred Bachofer (born 1942), former Lord Mayor of <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrtingen" title="Nürtingen">Nürtingen</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Adams_(athlete)" title="Walter Adams (athlete)">Walter Adams</a> (born 1945 in Wasseralfingen), middle distance runner</li>
<li>Ivo Holzinger (born 1948), politician (SPD), Lord Mayor of <a href="/wiki/Memmingen" title="Memmingen">Memmingen</a> (since 1980)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Werner_Sobek" title="Werner Sobek">Werner Sobek</a> (born 1953), architect and structural engineer</li>
<li>Ludwig Leinhos (born 1956), major general of the Bundesluftwaffe</li>
<li>Bernd Hitzler (born 1957), politician, (CDU), Member of Landtag</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Gerlach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Martin Gerlach (page does not exist)">Martin Gerlach</a> (born 1965), independent politician, mayor of Aalen (since 2005)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Zander_(wrestler)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Zander (wrestler)">Thomas Zander</a> (born 1967), wrestler, winner of Olympic silver medal and world champion (1994)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carl-Uwe_Steeb" title="Carl-Uwe Steeb">Carl-Uwe Steeb</a> (born 1967), retired tennis player</li>
<li>Katrin Bauerfeind (born 1982), radio and TV-presenter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manuel_Fischer" title="Manuel Fischer">Manuel Fischer</a> (born 1989), footballer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Funk" title="Patrick Funk">Patrick Funk</a> (born 1990), footballer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cro_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cro (rapper)">Cro</a> (born 1990), Carlo Waibel), singer</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aalen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart.jpg/120px-Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart.jpg" width="120" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart.jpg/180px-Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f3/Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="282" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Christian Friedrich Daniel Schubart</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christian_Friedrich_Daniel_Schubart" title="Christian Friedrich Daniel Schubart">Christian Friedrich Daniel Schubart</a> (1739–1791), poet, organ player, composer and journalist; lived in Aalen as a child and adolescent</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Duala_Manga_Bell" title="Rudolf Duala Manga Bell">Rudolf Duala Manga Bell</a> (1873–1914), King of Duala and resistance leader in the German colony of Kamerun, lived in Aalen from 1891 until 1896.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georg_Elser" class="mw-redirect" title="Georg Elser">Georg Elser</a> (1903–1945), opponent of Nazism, worked in 1923 as an apprentice carpenter in Aalen.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Werner_Bickelhaupt" title="Werner Bickelhaupt">Werner Bickelhaupt</a> (born 1939), football coach, lives in Aalen since 2004.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Thiele" title="Gerhard Thiele">Gerhard Thiele</a> (born 1953 in Heidenheim), physicist and former astronaut, attended school in Aalen.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andreas_Beck_(footballer)" title="Andreas Beck (footballer)">Andreas Beck</a> (born 1987 in Kemerovo/Soviet Union), German footballer, grew up in Aalen.</li>
</ul>
